<Rate>5<//Rate><Review>Went in expecting to spend 400 walked out spending 1400... Somehow I'm extremely happy.

1976 Bronco with a HO well built 5.0L. my exhaust headers we're a Miss match to Bronco and not only sit on the frame causing multiple gasket blow outs, but also impeded the clutch fork from actuating fully. On top of my header problem I had installed a new transmission set up that minimized three available space to run exhaust... I decided my 110VAC mig welder was not up to the task and I brought the rig into RPM.
Richard spent some decent time under the bronco with me as we discussed what I wanted as an endstate and how I wanted to get there. New ceramic headers built for my Bronco were not good enough and Richard had his guy custom weld the flang location to provide the absolute most clearance possible. Pipes were welded great and with real precision work keeping everything tight and tucked away.
Only problem was waiting on a gasket to get delivered by the local NAPA auto store that was overlooked, put a 2 hour delay on the whole thing making the total turn around from drop off to pick up <36 hours. Pretty damn good.

<text>I've been coming here or 6 months and it's been a decent experience. The facility is very clean (incredibly cold so bring a jacket or blanket!) and the staff has been nice and patient when helping me, I have not received any rude staff members as others have complained about.

You will wait a few hours on your first visit, so go on a day where you have absolutely nothing planned because you can wait from 4-6 hours although they tell you 2-4. Also, they can and will disqualify you for issues as small as asthma. So, ASK them first if you have medical issues before waiting so long. I've seen so many angry people scream and run out that door because they were disqualified after HOURS of waiting. ASK FIRST BEFORE WAITING!

Now Complaints...
They do seem understaffed on some days. The line will be going out the door which I really don't mind, it's when I'm finished that it's irritating. There were days where everyone would be finished at different times, and holding their hand up in their air ready leave for 20 minutes+ before staff came around. By then, EVERYONE begins to shout and claim that they were done first and whoever is the loudest or the closest to that staff member wins the game. If they had more staff members on the floor or even a number system instead of the hand raising thing, it would be less hostile and easier for both the donor and staff member.

My other complaint is some of the donors who go there. I've dealt with some short tempered hostile donors who try to fight for their place in line or fight to get unhooked from the IV and leave first, sometimes with me and sometimes with the staff. For the most part people are respectful but some of them are cranky and impatient and treat this place like it's there to only SERVE THEM but there's not really any way to avoid 'em.!</text>< name>
Andrea Duran< /name>

<Review>I have been donating at Octapharma regularly for about 4-6 months now. My time spent there has been a largely enjoyable experience. The staff is friendly and courteous, and this really says something considering how over-worked they are.

They could use more phlebotomists, but the ones there really know their stuff. And if you find a tech that you really like, they actually let you make requests. So if your favorite needle wizard is on duty, don‚Äôt be afraid to ask for their services.

Their registration while lengthy is actually streamlined so once you return the process goes much faster. This is of course all required by law and anyone criticizing them for this part of the procedure is simply ignorant of the fact that the staff & management cannot change this. Yes they are going to be collecting some very personal information, and yes some of your answers or a combination of them may disqualify you from donating‚Ä¶ Boo hoo.

This is not a retail service; you are not entitled to customer satisfaction. It is the staff‚Äôs foremost concern to protect the well being of their clients, and those who may be receiving donated plasma. For that reason they have to calculate the risk or chance that you may have some kind of disqualifying condition. Maybe your blood pressure is too low, too high, or maybe you engaged in & admitted to certain high risk behaviors. Either way, no one should be throwing daggers at an organization for complying with safety laws.

Wait times can be pretty long, but they are honest and forthright about this, telling every new customer that they can expect it to take between 2 and 3 hours. This is again, due to a lack of phlebotomists, and the popularity of this location. They are routinely swamped, with lines of beds full of people waiting their turn to get stuck. This is yet another thing that they as the company cannot control. They cannot wave a magical wand and produce a new tech with the same astounding level of skill I‚Äôve come to expect, nor can they banish the crowds of people that show up every day.

So yes the service, entirely because of circumstance, may be a little slow, but the quality is amazing.

The facilities are, well, unremarkable, but what do you expect, it‚Äôs a donation center. But it‚Äôs always very clean, and there are televisions positioned all around so you can always see one from any bed.

Their movie selection could use some serious, serious improvement however.</Review><user_id>113187095907647405660< /user_id>< Rate>
5< /Rate>
